# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

**Target Repositories (version-pinned mirrors):**

- `github.com/sg-evals/grafana--26d36ec` — use `repo:^github.com/sg-evals/grafana--26d36ec$` filter
- `github.com/sg-evals/grafana-loki` — use `repo:^github.com/sg-evals/grafana-loki$` filter
- `github.com/sg-evals/grafana-mimir` — use `repo:^github.com/sg-evals/grafana-mimir$` filter

Scope ALL keyword_search/nls_search queries to these repos.
Use the repo name as the `repo` parameter for read_file/go_to_definition/find_references.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

---

**Sourcegraph Repositories:** `github.com/sg-evals/grafana--26d36ec`, `github.com/sg-evals/grafana-loki`, `github.com/sg-evals/grafana-mimir`

# Grafana Alerting Rule Evaluation to Notification Chain

## Your Task

Trace how a Grafana unified alerting rule is evaluated and fired in grafana/grafana. Find Go source files implementing: the rule scheduler, the rule evaluation, the alert state transition, and the alert notification dispatch to receivers.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the crossrepo tracing domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/grafana--26d36ec.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/grafana--26d36ec` (grafana/grafana)
- `sg-evals/grafana-loki` (grafana/loki)
- `sg-evals/grafana-mimir` (grafana/mimir)

## Output Format

Create a file at `/workspace/answer.json` with your findings in the following structure:

```json
{
  "files": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go"}
  ],
  "symbols": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "SymbolName"}
  ],
  "chain": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "FunctionName"}
  ],
  "text": "Narrative explanation of your findings, citing repos and file paths."
}
```

Include only the fields relevant to this task. Your answer is evaluated against a closed-world oracle — completeness matters.

69-assistanttext-
Perfect! I've successfully traced the Grafana unified alerting rule evaluation and notification chain. The analysis has been saved to `/workspace/answer.json`.

## Summary

I've identified the complete flow of how a Grafana unified alerting rule is evaluated and fired:

### **Key Components:**

1. **Rule Scheduler** (`pkg/services/ngalert/schedule/schedule.go`)
   - Periodically fetches alert rules and schedules evaluations at configured intervals

2. **Rule Evaluation** (`pkg/services/ngalert/schedule/alert_rule.go` + `pkg/services/ngalert/eval/eval.go`)
   - Each alert rule is evaluated through the `evaluate()` method
   - Executes queries via the condition evaluator
   - Returns evaluation results

3. **Alert State Transition** (`pkg/services/ngalert/state/manager.go`)
   - `ProcessEvalResults()` processes evaluation results
   - `setNextStateForRule()` determines state transitions (Normal → Pending → Alerting → Resolved)
   - Manages state cache and persistence

4. **State Representation** (`pkg/services/ngalert/state/state.go`)
   - Tracks state lifecycle with timestamps (FiredAt, ResolvedAt)
   - Stores labels, annotations, and evaluation values

5. **Alert Notification Dispatch** (`pkg/services/ngalert/sender/router.go`)
   - Routes alerts based on organization configuration
   - Sends to internal or external Alertmanagers

6. **Organization-specific Alertmanager** (`pkg/services/ngalert/notifier/multiorg_alertmanager.go`)
   - Maps organizations to their Alertmanager instances
   - Handles alert ingestion via `PutAlerts()`

7. **External Dispatch** (`pkg/services/ngalert/sender/notifier.go` + `pkg/services/ngalert/sender/sender.go`)
   - Manages external Alertmanager connections
   - Batches and transmits alerts in Prometheus format

scheduling their evaluation at configured intervals.\\n\\n2. **Alert Rule Evaluation** (pkg/services/ngalert/schedule/alert_rule.go:run and evaluate): For each alert rule, the scheduler creates a goroutine that calls the evaluate() method. Calls setNextStateForRule() to determine the new state for each alert instance based on current and previous states\\n   - Handles state transitions (Normal, Pending, Alerting, ResolvedAt)\\n   - Creates StateTransition objects representing changes\\n   - Updates alert state cache and persists to database\\n\\n4. **Alert State Representation** (pkg/services/ngalert/state/state.go:State): Each alert instance maintains state including:\\n   - Current state (Normal, Pending, Alerting, Error, NoData)\\n   - Labels and annotations\\n   - FiredAt timestamp (when transitioned to Alerting)\\n   - ResolvedAt timestamp (when transitioned back to Normal)\\n\\n5. **Alert Notification Dispatch** (pkg/services/ngalert/schedule/alert_rule.go:send): After state processing:\\n   - State transitions are converted to PostableAlerts\\n   - Passed to AlertsSender interface (AlertsRouter implementation in pkg/services/ngalert/sender/router.go)\\n   - Router determines routing based on org configuration (internal Alertmanager vs external)\\n\\n6. **Organization-specific Alertmanager Routing** (pkg/services/ngalert/notifier/multiorg_alertmanager.go:AlertmanagerFor): The MultiOrgAlertmanager:\\n   - Maps each organization to its own Alertmanager instance\\n   - Routes alerts to the correct org's Alertmanager\\n\\n7. **Alert Ingestion** (pkg/services/ngalert/notifier/alertmanager.go:PutAlerts): The alertmanager receives alerts and:\\n   - Receives PostableAlerts with state transitions\\n   - Routes alerts through the Alertmanager's alert routing tree\\n   - Applies silences and inhibition rules\\n\\n8. **External Alertmanager Dispatch** (pkg/services/ngalert/sender/notifier.go:Manager and pkg/services/ngalert/sender/sender.go:ExternalAlertmanager):\\n   - For organizations with external Alertmanager configured, alerts are dispatched to external systems\\n   - Uses Prometheus-compatible alert format\\n   - Batches alerts for efficient transmission\\n\\nThe entire chain is coordinated in pkg/services/ngalert/ngalert.go (AlertNG service), which initializes and wires together all components: scheduler, evaluator factory, state manager, and alerting routers.\"\n}\n",
